Free Talk

A Laughing Matter, A Traveler from the Sea

Regular Customer in a Restaurant: I've been having lunch here every day this month. But today is the first time I've had a tender steak.

Waiter: Oh dear. I must have made a mistake. I gave you the steak that the boss eats.

Grandson: Grandfather, are you going to send off the old doctor at the university today?

Grandfather: What are you talking about? He won't wait for me to die before sending me off. Instead, he wants me to send him off?

Woman: Darling, do you love me or not?

Man: How can I not love you? Every time I hug you, I wish I could turn into a thousand-handed Guanyin. So that I can stretch out a thousand hands to hug you.

A: Women in the world will never understand the principles of economics. Therefore, they often do things that are not cost-effective.

B: That cannot be generalized. Give me an example.

A: My son swallowed a copper coin into his stomach the day before yesterday. My wife spent twelve yuan to ask a Western doctor to take it out for him. Spending twelve yuan for one copper coin. Isn't that too uneconomical?

Old Pastor: Aren't you satisfied enough? Don't you see that the gentleman next door has just lost his wife?

Henpecked Man: I'm always unhappy because I can't be like that gentleman next door.

Random Talks in the Capital by Lu Shu-yun

The Qinhuai River has been known as a land of beauties since ancient times. The Six Dynasties were filled with gold dust. In the south, the courtesans of the Changban Bridge and the Wuyi Lane made their names with songs and music. The pipa has aged. The enchanting scenery has been passed down as an anecdote. Ever since the Hongwu era, (Yu Tanxin's "Banqiao Miscellaneous Records" from Putian states that in the early years of Hongwu, sixteen buildings were built to house official courtesans. Light makeup and powder were used to welcome guests. It was called a romantic affair of the time, etc.). Five or six hundred years have passed with frequent changes and vicissitudes. The beauties have turned to yellow earth, the famous scholars to green shirts. A place of merriment has long been covered with lush grass. Scattered anecdotes and past events remain vaguely. Although the flowing customs of the Jiangzuo region have not faded away to this day, the guests and visitors from all over the world, selecting songs and beauties, after the Yang'a dance, are not as prosperous and splendid as they used to be. Now that the prohibition of prostitution is strictly enforced, the flower affairs have become even more desolate. The old courtyards and riverside pavilions have been turned into dusty markets. The painted boats of the Qinhuai River have been turned into floating homes for scholars. (In the old days, there were tea boats and painted boats moored in front of the Confucius Temple and in the Qinhuai River. The painted boats, such as Fuxing, Yuelai, and Desheng Taoyuan, all had carved railings and painted eaves, with horned lanterns on top. The skirts and hats, the sound of sheng and xiao, and the lights were dazzling. I saw them four or five years ago. Now, the phoenix has left the building empty, and it has all become the residence of ordinary people.) The bright moon is not constant, and the colorful clouds are easily scattered. The Six Dynasties are like a dream, and all that remains is to wander around. Those prostitutes in the old days who knew a little about music gathered in tea houses to sell their songs under the guise of "proofreading," thus avoiding the eyes and ears of the government. The tea houses in the Confucius Temple area also sold songs by female entertainers. The ban did not apply to them, and they profited from their singing and dancing, which were able to attract customers. They all competed to recruit them to run Qingchang. The lights of the Fanlou restaurant, with a profusion of silk and bamboo instruments, more than a dozen singers dressed up and took the stage, singing in response to each other, their pearly throats and fan shadows creating a drunken and mesmerizing atmosphere. From noon to midnight, the seats were always full, and the sound of sheng and xiao never ceased. Their prosperous careers have lasted for a long time without declining. This is because after the prohibition of prostitution, many of those who used to solicit customers have disappeared and hid, and dare not openly offer their smiles. On good days in spring and autumn, those who pursue pleasure recall the past, and there is no lack of emotion and sighing. It can be said that these few tea houses have become the only places of merriment. However, the beautiful women are in groups, and the powder and rouge are like clouds. Their beauty and skills are not uniform, and it is not easy to find those who are both beautiful and talented. For example, Li Lanfang of the Linfeng Pavilion, Zhang Xinhong and Lu Yanqiu of the Tianyun Tower, and Xiao Yu, who used to belong to the Qifang Pavilion and has now left Beijing, are all known for their graceful manners and mellow voices, and can be regarded as the leaders among their peers. Below Deng Kuai, they are just ordinary beauties. Recently, a certain small newspaper, under the pretext of appreciating art and promoting song and dance, has launched a "Capital Song and Dance Star Election." Their leisure and elegance have not been forgotten. I imagine that when the winners are announced and awarded with flowers, there will be a good story to add color to Qingxi and Baixia.

A Study of a Giant Fish by Xiu Jun

Regarding the giant fish in Hukou, it was mentioned in this newspaper on March 27 that a dead fish was found in the old lake area of Sheyang Lake, east of Funing, near the sea. It was shaped like a horse, more than ten feet tall, and weighed about three hundred piculs. It had no eyes. The nearby residents and fishermen were all surprised when they saw it. They competed to cut it up to fill their hunger for several days. The rest was sold to the towns and cities, and the proceeds were very large. In the past, people said that fish were the largest among aquatic creatures. I didn't believe it at first. Now that the fish in Hukou is so huge, I suddenly realized that what the ancients said was not false. In the midst of rising rice prices, this giant fish filled people's hunger for several days. It was not a bad thing to provide food for the poor. I have consulted ancient books, and there are quite a few similar giant fish. I have compiled and preserved them to aid in conversation. I have recorded them below.

The "Book of Han, Treatise on the Five Elements" says: In the third year of Jianping, a large fish appeared in Pingdu, Donglai. It was eight feet long and eleven feet tall. Seven of them died. The "Book of Later Han, Treatise on the Five Elements" says: In the second year of Xiping, two large fish appeared in the sea of Donglai. They were eight or nine zhang long and more than two zhang tall. The "Book of Wei" says: There is a Shuntian Temple on the ridge. In front of it is a fish bone with a hole in the middle through which a horse can ride in and out. "Miscellaneous Records" says: Li Deyu had a giant fish rib that was twenty-five feet long. It was engraved with the words: "Sent from the sea in the second year of Huichang." According to the "Hui Tong Zhi," in the second year of Kaicheng, there was a large fish that was six zhang long. It entered the Huai River from the sea and reached Haozhou. "Song Shi, Treatise on the Five Elements" says: In December of the first year of Zhidao, a large fish in Guangzhou struck the seawater and came out. The fish died. It was six zhang three chi long and more than one zhang tall. "Secret Chamber Idle Talk" says: Li Chongju saw a large fish on a sandy island in the sea. When he cut open its belly, he found a boat and three dead people. Their clothes were still complete. "Yu Jian" says: Shen Zuo Zhe once passed by the sea to Putuo Mountain. He saw flags and banners like tens of thousands of cavalry marching east from dozens of miles away in the sea. When he asked the locals, they said: "This is a large fish. The flags and banners are its scales." "Idle Talk of Farmers" says: During the Zhang family's reign, a sea fish fell in a town in Shanghai. It was nearly two zhang long and was called Kuoba. The "Fujian Tong Zhi" says: In the late Hongzhi period, a giant fish entered Jiudu, Zhangpu. When the tide receded, it could not leave. The villagers competed to cut its meat. At that time, they relied on it to survive the famine. The "Jiangnan Tong Zhi" says: In the twenty-sixth year of Jiajing, a large fish was caught at the mouth of Huapu, Suzhou. It had a horse's head and feet and weighed two thousand catties. The "Guangxi Tong Zhi" says: On July 23rd of the thirty-fifth year of Jiajing, a giant fish more than ten zhang long appeared and disappeared on the water surface in Taiping Prefecture. It lasted for three days. The carp's whiskers were all connected to its tail. Those who saw it were strange. The "Jiangnan Tong Zhi" says: In the spring of the twelfth year of Chongzhen, there were two large fish in Songjiang. They were dozens of zhang long, and their eyes could hold three people. They had no pupils. "Miscellaneous Records of Lenglu" says: The Dongyue Temple in Taizhou city has a fish bone orange. It is one chi wide and more than ten zhang long. It is medium flat. The two ends are curved and shaped like an orange. The temple keeper said that it was the tail bone of the fish. Its spine was even larger and was in a certain temple by the sea.

In summary, the dead fish found in Hukou is not yet considered huge. Its shape is like a horse, similar to the large fish at Huapu Port in Suzhou during the Jiajing period. Its height is more than ten zhang, similar to the large fish in Pingdu, Donglai. It has no eyes, similar to the two large fish in Songjiang during the Chongzhen period. The residents cut it up to fill their hunger, similar to the villagers of Jiudu, Zhangpu, during the Hongzhi period. It can be compared and mutually verified.

Common Sense Scraps - Light

When striking a match in the wind, it is often blown out. When it is lit, put it in the matchbox immediately, and there is no need to worry about it being blown out.

When walking on quiet roads such as Daxilu, it is best to be careful to prevent cars from speeding by and not being able to avoid them in time. Looking at car accidents, they often happen more often in quiet places than in busy places. This is clear evidence.

In terms of walking stability, rickshaws are not as good as cars, and cars are not as good as trams. The four words "cheap, comfortable, and beautiful" can be applied to trams without shame.

When you encounter a beggar following you on the road, you can cross to the opposite side of the road. The beggar will definitely retreat dejectedly, because each has its own territory.

Split a bamboo pen holder into two parts, sharpen the lower end into a shovel shape, and then embed a soft brush in it. You can make two straight brushes for drawing.

Travelogue of Nanyang (3) - Spiritual Flower

On the fourth day, I had a good dream. I dreamed that the moon emitted light, illuminating my heart. I wrote a poem in my dream. In my dream, I saw the bright moon, its flowing light illuminating my heart. The moon emitted a strange glow, truly the Goddess of Mercy. Auspicious light shone on my head, entering deep into my heart and spleen. I understood the riddle of the mother and child, proving it to this day. Ten, hundred, thousand, ten thousand, the earth transforms into gold. On the fifth day, I visited the New World, which was similar to Shanghai, but on a much smaller scale. There were also movies and Chinese opera, and many tourists. The price was one or two corners. There was a merry-go-round, which was very interesting. A circular machine moved, and the people in the seats straddled the wooden horses and moved up and down. The shape was not fixed to a horse, or in a fish or shrimp. The movement was random. I said, "This is also the six paths of reincarnation, where gods and humans live apart. But cause and effect are certain, and the body follows the cycle and is not free." Shanghai and Japan both have this game.

On the sixth day, I gave a lecture at Yangzheng Middle School, titled "The True Value of Greater Chinese Culture and Its Mission in the 20th Century." It was roughly based on the history of Eastern and Western cultures, proving that Western national culture does not have the ability to dominate the world, but Eastern national culture does. The mission of unifying the world into a great community in the 20th century lies especially with the Chinese. This article is of great importance, so I have recorded it below.

The British Confucian scholar Darwin said that humans evolved from apes. This is a long time ago, at least 100,000 years ago. We won't talk about that. Let's just say that 10,000 years ago, Europeans only knew how to use stones. Later, they learned to use bones. For example, the bone flute was created in a time that can be recorded. The Africa of Egypt can be traced back to 5400 BC. There are pyramids to examine. But my Fu Xi dynasty was already in 2953 BC. And in 1000 BC, the West, although it had no history, already knew how to use iron, which they learned from the East. The so-called East refers to the area of Asia Minor. In the 12th and 13th centuries AD, Westerners began to know about coal and called it burning stones. The history of Greece can be recorded back to the 7th century BC. The 6th century BC was the era when Sakyamuni Buddha and Lao Tzu were born. The golden age of Greece was in the 4th century BC. Solon 6362丨558 was a sage and legislator of Greece. He studied abroad with monks in Africa and Egypt. The monks taught him, "You Greeks are the younger generation and have no place to speak." Even the Western alphabet Abphabeto was passed from Egyptian Phoenician merchants to Greece. In 466 BC, the Greek sage Felix brought about the golden age of Greece. His achievements can be compared to the Duke of Zhou in China. However, he received a great deal of Eastern academic culture. Many scholars went from a place called Ionia in the southwest corner of Asia Minor to Greece. The Ionian school of philosophy was originally in a place called Miletus in Asia Minor. Therefore, it is also called the Miletus school. Famous philosophers include Thaleso (640-500 BC), Anaximenes (910-542 BC), and Anaxagoras (approximately 550-246 BC). Several of his disciples explained that the elements of the universe are composed of water, that the universe comes from the Infinite, and that it is transformed from one energy. They went to Greece to spread the Tao and were the creators of the first phase of Greek philosophy. The last one was a friend of the Duke of Zhou of Greece, Felix. Not only did male philosophers go to Greece to be pioneers, but even female philosophers went from the East. For example, the highest confidential female advisor to the Duke of Zhou of Greece was the female sage Aspasia. She was not only Felix's confidante, but their relationship was even deeper than that of Felix's wife. She was also from Asia Minor. This Miss Ya was not only Felix's advisor, but also a friend of the three Greek sages Socrates and Plato. She once advised Felix to change from autocracy to a republic. She can be considered the only female sage in ancient and modern times. She was also an Asian who went to educate Europeans. This is the old source of Eastern and Western culture in the first era of Greece.

The description of not having pupils corresponds. The residents cut it up to fill their hunger, similar to the villagers of Jiudu, Zhangpu, during the Hongzhi period. They can be cross-referenced and mutually verified.

Interesting Stories of Mailmen by Lü Bing

There was a certain mailman in England who was naturally a heavy sleeper. He had to report to work at four o'clock every night, but he often missed the time. He was repeatedly warned but did not change his ways. Therefore, his superiors warned him that if he did not change his habits, he would be dismissed. The mailman's family specially prepared two alarm clocks, which rang on time. However, the loud sound was not enough to drive away the sleeping demon. Sometimes, the mailman even slept without taking off his boots, so that he could save himself the trouble of putting them on in a hurry. Unexpectedly, after a year, this mailman was suddenly able to report to work on time as scheduled, almost becoming a model for the entire staff. According to his own account, he would set the alarm clock every night. The other end of the clock controlled the opening and closing of a spring. When the bell rang, the movement of the hammer would cause the water tank near his head to open freely, and cold water would pour on his neck. He woke up unexpectedly. This method actually worked. The joy of the mailman can be imagined.

Later, the mailman got married. He had someone next to him in bed, but she did not necessarily have the same habit of heavy sleeping. Therefore, he earnestly instructed his wife to wake him up on time. However, he still did not think it was completely reliable, so he continued to follow the old method and use the water tank. Unexpectedly, when it rang on time, cold water flowed straight down. The wife, who was lying beside him, was greatly affected. As a result, she was ashamed to go to work at the bureau, because her face already showed the claw marks of his wife.

The above facts are enough for interesting talk, so I recorded them in Jackson's new book, entitled "History of Mailman Aviation," because it is full of humor, so I translated it to tell the readers of "Free Talk."

Warmth in the Heart (1) (8) (1) Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: The Burning Flames Soar to the Sky, Goulan Praises the Filial Son, Red Carpet Laid on the Ground, Meeting Famous Actors on the Spot

At this time, Zuo Shichen thought, "Liu Xingshu's family is not very wealthy. With a poor family style, and an engagement ring that costs four or five hundred yuan, it seems that five thousand yuan is not enough. But being too shabby is not good. It's really like what Xingshu said, the Fang family has married off several daughters, and there is a comparison. Even if it can't be the best in comparison, it can't be the worst. Like tax officials, there is also a comparison, and it can't be too far off." At that time, Liu Xingshu felt a little financially strained, but he was very happy. Zuo Shichen was his good friend and could talk about anything, but he couldn't dampen his spirits. He was originally a pessimistic person, but now he was happy because of his marriage, which was rare. He said that he had no savings and was afraid of having to borrow money, but his father was in the same circle, and several of their relatives were also in the financial world, so it would be easy to move around, and he didn't need to worry too much. It's just that he would have to bear a heavier burden in the future. While Liu Xingshu's marriage was in progress, his brother Liu Yinmen also returned from Europe and was about to get married. The Chinese used to have an old custom that if there were several brothers in a family, it seemed most appropriate to get married in order. Otherwise, relatives and friends would have suspicions. The same was true for sisters' marriages. Therefore, there was a saying, "If the older sister doesn't marry, it delays the younger sister." It seems that if the older sister is not married, it is not appropriate to arrange a marriage for the younger sister. Nowadays, this is not strictly observed. In the past, order was very important. After Yinbo returned, someone made a match for him. It was also a coincidence that this marriage was also related to the Fang family. That young lady was Fang's nephew, and the cousin of Xingshu's fiancée. It turned out that when Liu Yinbo was studying in Europe, the minister to Belgium was Fang Erxiansheng. He wanted to find a young man with talent and intelligence among the students, and Liu Yinbo happened to be related to the Fang family and knew that Liu Yinbo was not yet married, so naturally he was chosen. Before returning to China, although he had this intention, he did not talk about it, because the group of students studying abroad naturally had a higher vision than ordinary young people. They often had ideal figures, with certain conditions. Moreover, they had breathed foreign air, and perhaps they already had someone in their hearts. Although there were very few female students studying abroad at that time, there were also some who were unable to find qualified women in China, and even some who married foreign wives. It was not unheard of. Therefore, Minister Fang, although he had this intention, did not say it, because he wanted to wait until Liu Yinbo returned to China before speaking.

Domestic Interest on Deposits Opened

Agreed at Five Taels

Whenever long-term loans are due, the silver houses and banks hold a meeting to discuss the interest rates on deposits, generally based on the overall market situation to determine the level. This year, the money market is more relaxed than in previous years, so the interest rate on domestic deposits must be lowered. It was agreed at five taels the day before yesterday, which is 2.5 cents less than the previous period (the end of last year). Those who have relationships with depositors and need to add 5 cents or 1 tael are still allowed, so the maximum is no more than six taels. It is found that the amount of long-term deposits absorbed by money houses this time is far less than the amount of the previous period, because the large number of deposits from customers have been replaced with new accounts. According to the investigation, in addition to the self-use funds left for other business operations, most of them are deposited in Chinese banks. Whether the interest rate is increased depends on the quality of the account and the size of the funds. It is also heard that yesterday, Ningbo houses released more than 3 million in long-term loans due at the end of the month, and the houses in this street also made 4-5 million. It is estimated that the total amount made in the past few days is more than 10 million.

Grain Prices: River Rice Market in Irreversible Decline

Overall Market Remains Dull and Soft

Zhabei: Yesterday, the arrival of goods at various wharves was slightly improved, but the accumulated stock in the river was still substantial. Sales in Shanghai were sluggish, as stores were already well-stocked and observing the market. Additionally, competition from foreign rice put pressure on the market. As a result, transactions for white japonica rice were exceptionally quiet. Prices fluctuated due to a lack of high-quality goods and the abundance of inferior goods. Yesterday afternoon, there were few buyers for medium-quality japonica rice in Zhongguan, and the overall market softened further. Top-quality japonica rice was still in demand, while thin paddy rice was firm for high-quality goods and weak for inferior goods. Although the quantity of goods was not large, the market was strange and dull. Glutinous rice and Xian rice transactions were weak. In recent times, the Xian rice market has been virtually nonexistent, but prices have been quite firm. Alcohol distilleries were the only slight purchasers of substandard glutinous rice, and prices initially fell before stabilizing.

Hunan, Shanghai: Approximately ten boats arrived from the river. Changzhou and Wuxi japonica rice from the north of the street were still active, and prices were stable. Su and Tong japonica rice sales were sluggish, and the market was quite poor. High-quality goods were unchanged, while medium and inferior goods softened slightly, with an estimated fluctuation of half a jiao. A small number of merchants inquired about early thin paddy rice from Nanbang, and bids were extremely tight. Top-quality goods were sold as soon as they arrived, while inferior goods inevitably suffered price cuts. Glutinous and pointed rice from the south are currently in very short supply, and transactions are quiet. Sales of white glutinous rice were very sluggish. Although a portion was inquired about in the street, the owners refused due to the excessive discounts. Market prices were nominally flat but actually weak, with buyers and sellers excluding each other.

Delivery Approaching, Near-Term Noodles Weaken Further

Distant Months Buck the Trend Due to Weather

Yesterday's noodle market saw near-term months weaken while distant months remained stable in both the morning and afternoon. December, nearing delivery, saw no movement in actual sales. Although major manufacturers did not have short positions, there were still many chips from manufacturers with short positions. At a time when sales were not improving, it was difficult for bulls to cope with the pressure from a small number of actual sellers. Therefore, floating longs closed out positions at any time, while shorts also took the opportunity to cover. However, the trend inevitably weakened slightly. Distant months were initially flat and weak, but in the afternoon, with light rain again due to weather, speculative and long-oriented buyers became active again, and each contract saw a slight rebound. However, small and medium-sized manufacturers were still offering positions for May and June, because they expected the outcome of the current month to be similar to that of the previous month. Therefore, the future trend of near-term weakness and distant stability seems to be already visible. As a result, the closing price for the current month was down another two and a half li compared to the previous week, May was up two and a half li, June and July were up seven and a half li, and August and September were up five li.

Spot Wheat Demand Weak, Prices Fall by Five Fen

Light Rain Boosts Futures Market Slightly

Yesterday's wheat market saw each month open flat and then firm up. In the morning, with cloudy weather but no rain, quotations for foreign wheat fluctuated by one or two jiao, so sentiment was still stable. However, when the afternoon opened, light rain began to fall again, and speculative sentiment revived. Inland areas such as the Xibang were very firm due to the intermittent rain, so a sharp drop in the market still seemed unlikely. As a result, June rebounded three fen compared to the previous week, and July, August, and September each rose two fen. Over 5,000 bags of spot wheat were traded, but bids were down five fen from the previous weekend, because manufacturers were reporting poor noodle sales and weak demand for wheat, resulting in a market where prices were gradually falling and supply greatly exceeded demand. Five liang of wheat from Xuzhou, Qingjiangpu, Suzhou, and Bengbu were purchased by Fufeng.

Silk and Tea: Shanghai Factories Experience Sharp Drop of 30-40 Taels

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign silk market experienced a sharp drop because overseas inventories were large and sales decreased, and the Yokohama raw silk market was weak. Shanghai's new cocoon raw silk was still rarely offered. Although aged cocoon silk was being offered, European firms suppressed prices and hoarded it. Yesterday, Qianli and others imported 40 bales of Shanghai white factory raw silk, and prices fell by 30-40 taels. Zhonghe imported 20 bales of white dried raw silk, and prices also tended to weaken.

Early Silkworms in Western Zhejiang Will Soon Be Thriving

Expect Opening Around the Beginning of Next Month... Unfavorable Weather Makes a Bountiful Harvest Difficult to Expect. In the Jinan, Lanxi, Yuhang and other districts of western Zhejiang, the spring silkworm breeding quantity of farmers this year is not weak. At the beginning of the silkworm season, conditions were still good. After the third sleep, silkworm farmers felt difficulties in breeding due to the impact of unfavorable weather. Many silkworms were found to be diseased and abandoned. Now, early silkworms will be sleeping and thriving, and we only hope that the weather will turn sunny and warm immediately, and that they can be put on the cluster in four or five days at the latest. Silkworm houses in each district have scheduled separate openings on the fifth day of the next month. Whether the harvest will be bountiful or poor depends on the weather. This week is the most important time for the silkworm season, and silkworm farmers are full of worries.

New Local Green Tea Is on the Market

Yesterday, Yuancheng Yong Tea Shop displayed 37 boxes of new local Zhenmei tea samples. The rough tea was purchased from Hangzhou and produced by Yitongxing Tea Shop. The fragrance and manufacturing method are excellent. After English firms reviewed them, it was heard that Jardine had already sent telegrams. Although British firms had counter-offered, the difference was too great and no transaction was made. Observing the situation from all sides, the opening is still some time away.

Recent Tea News from Tunxi and Wuyuan

Tea Houses in Tunxi Are Mostly Observing the Issue of Opening

Wuyuan Expects Pessimistic Views Due to High Costs

Tunxi is the central location of Huixiu and Shexian tea markets. There are no less than 70 tea houses in this town and in Shuikou, Liyang, Yanghu, and other places. This year, most of the old tea houses, except for a portion that has prepared to open, are mostly observing. The reason for this is that there is no guarantee that foreign sales will be smooth. Although sales to Russia have recovered, the prices offered are extremely low, barely covering transportation, tax, and decoration costs. Chinese merchants are losing no less than 40 taels per dan. Additionally, tea houses are tightening the release of remittances, and money is tight inland, so mountain prices cannot be suppressed. In view of these difficulties, tea houses have not been as enthusiastic as in previous years. Recently, Tunxi has had plenty of cash, and ticket prices have fallen back to 1,380 yuan compared to the beginning of the month. Whether tea houses in Tunxi will increase depends on the rise and fall of ships in Shanghai.

Wuyuan's green tea is of high quality, and mountain costs are generally higher than elsewhere. This year, due to soaring rice prices and doubled commodity prices, it takes 30 workers to pick and bake each dan of tea, costing 27 yuan in wages, 7 yuan for meals, 10 yuan for firewood, and 5 yuan for miscellaneous items. The usual cost of cultivation is 10 yuan, totaling about 60 yuan, an increase of 15 yuan per dan compared to the past. At first, each tea house still hoped that mountain prices would decrease. Based on the cost of these mountain households, each dan would have to be 80 yuan or more when it opens in the future. Therefore, tea houses, seeing these mountain prices, are even more pessimistic about the future due to the heavy cost of making finished boxes.

British Tea Merchants Restricting Production

Since 1925, the production of tea in India and Java has increased sharply from 20 million dan to 40 million dan. Although the London market has a large appetite, supply greatly exceeds demand. With ample inventory, tea prices have fallen sharply, and tea merchants are in a precarious situation. Now, British tea merchants have unanimously agreed to strictly limit production from this year onwards in order to maintain the tea industry.

Piece Goods: Hangzhou Merchants Search for Fine Cloth Spot

Local Factory Cloth Prices Rose Again Yesterday. This was because the goods needed to cover silver at the end of the month had mostly been sold off, and Hangzhou merchants were again searching for fine cloth spot in a big way. Yesterday was the last day, so over 200 pieces were transported, bought and loaded on the spot, and prices rose by 2.5 to 5 fen. Ningbo merchants imported over 100 pieces of 11-pound coarse cloth, and prices also firmed up. However, there was still no improvement in the situation for the Yangtze merchants. The Jiangxi and Anqing ports with the greatest demand were lacking enthusiasm. Yesterday, Guangzhou merchants imported 150 pieces of fine diagonal cloth, priced at 6 liang 9 qian 2.5 fen. Northern merchants were experiencing sluggish imports due to the unsettled situation.

East and West Piece Goods Trends Are Disordered. Eastern goods are affected by the Zhongyuan factory strike, and some goods are particularly scarce, such as Changbanqiao Zhigong Ni, Baokiu, Bald Blue Gray, and Jiji. These goods will not arrive until the strike is resolved. Moganshan Zhigong Ni also rose by 2.5 li, opening yesterday at 2 qian 7 fen. Printed cloth is increasingly falling due to sluggish Indian sales, resulting in a flood of shipments to China. Yesterday, dark-colored Chongshen was only selling for 3 liang 9 qian 5 fen, and white-ground cloth was 3 liang 9 qian, with little sales. Actual sales to Sichuan and Han merchants were still dull. Ningbo merchants added slightly to their purchases. Over 20 pieces of Western glass yarn were imported yesterday. Maolong Four Heroes were 2 qian 4 fen, and Huaji Jubaopen were 2 qian 3.5 fen.

Sugar Market: Domestic Blue and Red Sugar Scarce and Popular

Coarse Sand White Sugar Market Quiet and Weak

Yesterday, sugar market telegraphs from production areas indicated that Cuban spot sugar and New York futures sugar showed no rise or fall. The price of Javanese spot sugar was 10 guilders, and the price of May futures sugar was 10.125, both down by 125. June saw no rise. There was still little buying interest in Shenggonghui sand white sugar, and the market appeared weak, with a transaction price of 7 liang 2 qian. High-quality goods reached 2 qian 5 fen. The market was slow. Japanese sugar N brand was 7 liang 7 qian, YP brand was 7 liang qian 5 fen, and YRO brand was 7 liang 3 qian. Transactions were not many, and the market was stable. Only over 100 bags of Mianhu red sugar were sold, priced at 7 liang 6 qian. Inventory was scarce, and the market was still popular. Yellow Gang Blue sugar was still lacking on the market, and even inferior inventory was thin. Therefore, Banan Blue continued to be sold off for days, and prices remained as before. The market gradually became more lively.

Miscellaneous News: A box of gold bars was transported from Hankou to Shanghai, worth 100,000 yuan.

1,249 pieces of Indian ramie and 25 pieces of ramie bags were imported yesterday.

6,100 barrels of cement and 700 pieces of Western paper were shipped from the United States to Shanghai.

82 boxes of dried scallops were shipped from Southeast Asia.

580 boxes of matches were shipped from Japan to Shanghai.

1,500 pieces of American cotton and 15,018 pieces of Indian cotton have arrived in Shanghai.

880 bags of wheat were shipped from Shashi to Shanghai.

New Qingchuan fish was offered by Shanghai Commercial Bank yesterday for three weeks of forward delivery of 4,000 boxes at a price of 5 liang 4 qian.

According to a telegram from Kobe, agar-agar is scarce and the market is tight, and various shops continue to raise prices by 10 yuan.

Local News

Grand Ceremony for the Inauguration of the Shanghai Municipal Executive and Supervisory Committee Members

Held Yesterday on the Third Floor of the Municipal Party Headquarters

Cai Yuanpei Represented the Central Government as the Overseer

The second Shanghai Special Municipality Executive and Supervisory Committee members, already selected by the Central Government and officially begun their duties, held an oath-taking ceremony yesterday at 10 AM in the City Party Headquarters auditorium. Mr. Cai Yuanpei was dispatched by the Central Government to represent and oversee the oath-taking. Following a report by Chairman Chen Dezheng, the Executive and Supervisory Committee members took their oaths. Subsequently, the Central Government representative delivered an address, with speeches also given by Mayor Zhang Yuejun, Ye Huijun of the Chamber of Commerce Preparatory Committee, and Tan Yigong of the Lawyers' Association. Finally, Pan Gongzhan delivered a response on behalf of the Executive and Supervisory Committee members. Representatives from various organizations, groups, and party branches at all levels attended as observers, numbering in the hundreds. The ceremony was grand, and details are as follows:

Meeting Staff: (Presidium) Chen Dezheng, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Yansong; (Record) Hu Yanyun; (Master of Ceremonies) Xu Yefu; (Piano) Lin Kecong; (Reception) Chen Jianzong, Jiang Zhenwu; (Affairs) Zhang Tianbai, etc.

Committee Members Taking the Oath: Executive Committee Members: Chen Dezheng, Pan Gongzhan, Tao Baichuan, Tong Xingbai, Fan Zhengbo, Chen Junyi, Yang Qingyuan, Wu Bokuan, Alternate Executive Committee Members: Hou Dachun, Huang Xuchu, Zhou Feicheng, Bao Rong, Cai Hongtian; Supervisory Committee Members: Zhu Yingpeng, Xiong Shihui, Chen Xizeng, Wang Yansong, Deng Tongwei; Alternate Supervisory Committee Members: Wu Xiu, Jiang Huaisu.

Ceremony Order: (1) Music and opening; (2) Sing the Party Anthem; (3) Pay the highest respects to the Party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; (4) Chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will (Wang Yansong); (5) Three minutes of silence; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Central Government Overseer takes position; (8) Executive and Supervisory Committee members take oaths; (9) Central Party Headquarters representative delivers an address; (10) Guests deliver speeches; (11) Executive and Supervisory Committee member representative delivers a response; (12) Shout slogans; (13) Photography; (14) Music and adjournment.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Chen Dezheng delivered the opening address, saying: "Central Government representative, esteemed guests, comrades, today the Executive Committee and Supervisory Committee members of the Chinese Kuomintang Shanghai Special Municipality are taking their oaths of office here. These Executive Committee and Supervisory Committee members were produced from the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang Shanghai Special Municipality. During the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress, meticulous and complete instructions were given regarding party affairs, politics, and other work. From these thorough resolutions, the Executive and Supervisory Committee members taking office have a clear path to strive towards. On this day of taking the oath, I would like to provide a comprehensive and concise report on our work over the past year to the Central Government representative, esteemed guests, and comrades. The environment of the past year had too great an impact on us. The work of the Municipal Party Headquarters was mostly in responding to events, with the actual work often wanting to be attended to but circumstances not allowing it. After the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress, we have well-organized steps and plans in advance to ensure that all matters will be completely realized under predetermined plans. In terms of party affairs, there are four main objectives: organization, propaganda, training, and mass training. All four aspects received thorough instructions at the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress. In terms of organization, we are proceeding step by step according to the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress. Within a year, we can make the party organization in Shanghai comprehensive and successful. Not only will the district branches and party departments be comprehensive, but every comrade will be able to be a vanguard of the party. Comrades, under a comprehensive organization like a net, will operate flexibly, acting as the arm is controlled by the body and the finger is controlled by the arm. In terms of propaganda, the impact of the past environment was too great. Temporary events often occurred, leaving us overwhelmed, so that the work of the party could not be fully implemented according to the initial plan, going to the people and delving into the masses. Now we must not only expand propaganda but also delve into the people, so that everyone believes in the ideology and obeys the will of the party. This is certainly what we should strive for, but it is also a point we hope everyone will often instruct us on. In terms of training, little training work was done in the early stages. Only in the past year has training work been highlighted. Now we want to enable every party member to accept the party's orders and obey the party's will. In terms of education, the education sector must earnestly implement in accordance with the party's ideology. We have plans to ensure that party member training and party ideology education will both have considerable achievements within a year. As for mass training, we know that this work is the most difficult to do in Shanghai, because Shanghai has a large population, a mix of Chinese and foreigners, and complex elements. However, while difficulty cannot be avoided, difficulty is also our best opportunity from the party's perspective. We must use the party's will to overcome difficulties. In the past, there were many strange and bizarre events. In the future, we must not only make the mass organizations comprehensive but also make the masses obey the party's orders and accept the party's will to implement them. We originally intended to strive along this path, and we especially hope that everyone can jointly assist us. Today, there is much more to say about the party, but for the sake of time, I can only mention the important points here. Regarding politics, it is also okay to say a little more. In an era of saving the country through the party, governing the country through the party, and building the country through the party, the party's responsibility for politics is greater than in any other time or country. The party has the responsibility to supervise and examine politics. In the past, the Shanghai political authorities were able to present all their work to the public, even making the public satisfied, because of the efforts of the authorities and the success of party-government unity. On the government's side, it was believed that political work was the work of the party. On the party's side, it was believed that the work of the party was to support the work of the government. Therefore, there are many events that Shanghai has achieved that other places have not. I dare to believe that if this continues, the government will naturally recognize that political work is the work of the party, and the party will naturally recognize that the work of the party is to support the work of the government. Then, the six years of political tutelage will certainly be completed earlier than in any other place. This is the success of overcoming all complex forces with the strength of party-government unity. Therefore, in the future, as long as we strive according to the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress, the future success will certainly be greater than in the past. In addition, there are many other things that the Sixth Congress entrusted to us. We hope that everyone will help us to fully realize them. What we hope from the Central Government representative, esteemed guests, and comrades is, first, that all comrades will supervise us at all times, so that those who are taking office here today will never forget the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress. What we ask of all comrades is that the strength of these Executive and Supervisory Committee members taking office is limited, and we must have the concerted assistance of all comrades and the entire citizenry so that no difficulties arise in the execution of the resolutions. This is the first point. Secondly, Shanghai has a large population and complex circumstances. If you say that Shanghai has many nests of reactionary forces and many obstacles to our work, we hope that everyone will remove a difficulty on the negative side, which is to help the Municipal Party Headquarters complete a task on the positive side. This is the second point. Thirdly, everyone's energy is used to deal with the reactionaries. Therefore, at this time, we especially hope that everyone will pay attention to the activity of the reactionaries and rise up to expose them, so that the work of the party can proceed smoothly and everyone's energy can be concentrated on construction work. This is the third point. There is also one more point: in the past, there were often situations where comrades could not understand each other. This kind of mutual suspicion invisibly reduces the strength of the revolution. We believe that only with the strength of the revolution can the city's culture and politics develop, and only with the strength of the revolution can the people live and work in peace and contentment. Therefore, we hope that everyone will no longer engage in meaningless attacks and slanders, and that they will jointly assist this Executive and Supervisory Committee in implementing the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress. In short, the Executive and Supervisory Committee has only twenty or so members, and their strength is limited. However, it is also very easy to make their strength great, which requires the assistance of all comrades. If everyone can assist the Executive and Supervisory Committee with all their heart, their strength will be great; otherwise, not much strength can be found. The above few shallow words are what I, on behalf of all the Executive and Supervisory Committee members, sincerely tell everyone, and they are also the few points I hope for from everyone. Finished."

Representative's Address: Central Representative Cai Yuanpei's instructional address roughly stated: "Today is the inauguration ceremony of all of you committee members, and Yuanpei has been ordered by the Central Government to oversee it. The position of the Shanghai Party Headquarters is unmatched in importance except for the capital. Shanghai is a very complex place. Before the revolutionary army reached the Yangtze River basin, Shanghai already had many comrades undertaking very important work. After the revolutionary army arrived, they still did not slacken. All of you committee members have been very diligent in the past. Chairman Chen's report on the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress is already known to the Central Government. The Central Government is very satisfied with such preparation for a year's work. In the circumstances of Shanghai, the most important thing is the training of the masses. We must train every member of the masses to have the qualifications of a party member. The Central Government has discovered the mistakes in Guangdong and Wuhan in the past and is actively striving to work practically, such as the regulations for afforestation, literacy, and other movements, which will be carried out separately by the provincial and municipal party headquarters to the county party headquarters and district branches. Also, during the period of political tutelage, it is necessary to train the masses in the exercise of the four powers, so that in the future, the period of constitutional government can be reached. However, in activities such as afforestation and literacy, it is imperative to make the masses aware of the consequences of not having forests, such as future disasters, and the relationship between forests and water conservancy. Everything must be thoroughly understood by them. The reason why they do not understand is that they do not know our propaganda. For example, training the masses to exercise the four powers solely by relying on spoken language will have limited effectiveness, and many legal provisions cannot be translated into spoken language. Sun Yat-sen also saw this in the early days of the party, so he wanted to teach the people to read. The literacy movement is the most important work to start during the period of political tutelage. The phonetic symbols recently passed by the Education Conference and decided by the Central Government are the best tool for literacy, because it is very difficult to promote literacy only using the current characters. Even in the case of the Thousand Character Classic, there are still very few who can read newspapers and books after finishing the Thousand Character Classic. Phonetic symbols are a method invented by Mr. Wu Jingheng. First, teach them to use local pronunciations to annotate the sounds, and it will be easy to read. After the masses can recognize phonetic symbols, the work during the period of political tutelage will be easier to carry out. First, promote it from the district branches to nearby households, and gradually promote it to the entire citizenry. It is very convenient. Today, there is nothing to guide the committee members in Shanghai. I have especially presented the new phonetic symbols decided by the Central Government to everyone, hoping that in addition to implementing the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress, everyone will pay attention to this literacy tool."

Committee Member's Response: Pan Gongzhan, representing the Executive and Supervisory Committee members, delivered a response, saying: "Today, the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive and Supervisory Committee members are taking their oaths of office. We are very grateful for the guidance from the Central Government representative, esteemed sirs, and comrades regarding the work we should do in the future. At the same time, we will summarize what everyone has said and use it as a compass for the work of the Executive and Supervisory Committee in the coming year. First, regarding the method specially proposed by Central Government Representative Cai, which is to use phonetic symbols in the literacy movement, we believe that only literacy can open up the people's minds, and the training of the four powers must also begin with the development of the people's minds. At the same time, we believe that it is impossible to develop the people's minds using the existing characters. For example, if you put up a slogan saying 'Those who are illiterate cannot be citizens,' or even 'Those who are illiterate cannot be people,' who are you showing it to? Showing it to those who are literate? They don't need to see it. Showing it to those who are illiterate? They simply can't see it. Therefore, using characters to make people literate is a dream. Only using phonetic symbols can achieve this goal. The Central Government has now decided to use phonetic symbols as a tool for propaganda and education. Mr. Cai has especially raised this point, and we solemnly accept and abide by it. We also have a statement to make, which is that in the past, many party affairs workers regarded work as the work of the party headquarters, rather than the work of the party. For example, today, they receive a few official documents and send a few official documents, regardless of the actual efficiency for the people. For example, the literacy movement is the work of the party and is one of the seven movements stipulated by the Central Government. If you use the strength of the party headquarters alone, it will not succeed. Among the 2.8 million people in Shanghai, there are no fewer than hundreds of thousands who are illiterate. Relying solely on the strength of the party headquarters personnel to teach them to read will certainly not be enough. You must first have all the party members in the city fully understand phonetic symbols, and then use all the party members in the city to teach the masses they are close to, and then rely on this part of the masses who have already become literate to lead the rest of the people who are not yet literate to become literate in order to succeed. This is just using literacy as an example. All work should be done in the same way. For example, the tree planting movement, if only representatives plant a few trees every year, that's how it will be in ten years or a hundred years, and Shanghai will still have those few trees. Therefore, you must specify a time for everyone to make efforts separately, and then there is hope for success. At the same time, we heard Mayor Zhang say that in the past year, the reactionary forces in Shanghai have been very rampant, but there has been no major trouble, which is due to party-government cooperation. Therefore, in the future, the party and the government must be completely like one family. Regarding the people, Mr. Ye said that 2.8 million people are locked in a bamboo garden with no way out, and the Executive and Supervisory Committee members must lead them out. This responsibility is too great, and our strength is too small. However, since we have been elected as Executive and Supervisory Committee members, we should strive to shoulder this responsibility. However, before the concessions in Shanghai are recovered, the environment is complex, and many matters cannot be as easy as we hope. There must be non-swearers among the people who come out, accept the intentions of the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive and Supervisory Committee, and lead other people to find a way out of the bamboo garden. We know that the most difficult thing is the middle way, but it is also the most stable. Headlong rushing is the easiest. Therefore, we can only follow the path of the Central Government, not to the left or to the right, and follow the teachings of Sun Yat-sen. Not only can we lead all the people in Shanghai, but we can also lead the people of the whole country. Now that there is a bright light ahead, we must also light up street lights along the way so that the people can advance on the middle way. Therefore, we not only have party-government cooperation and abide by the intentions of the Central Government to implement the resolutions of the Sixth All-Shanghai Congress, but we also want to make our work and our strength deeply penetrate into the midst of the people, and that is what this means."

Political and Military Authorities

Announcement Maintaining Public Security

Strikes, School Closures, and Mass Demonstrations are Prohibited

The Shanghai Special Municipality Government and the Songhu Garrison Headquarters jointly issued an announcement, stating: "Regarding the matter of the announcement, now is a time of military affairs, and the public security of the rear is extremely important. According to secret reports, the Communist Party and the reactionaries are taking the opportunity to cause disturbances and plan to incite strikes, hold demonstrations, and implement riots in May. In order to consolidate public security and prevent the sprout of chaos, hereafter, all sectors must not have strikes, school closures, or mass demonstrations. Various commemorative meetings in May, if not led by the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters, should also be prohibited. Those who deliberately violate this will be punished by military law for disrupting the rear, and will not be leniently treated. In addition to ordering the military police to strictly investigate, this announcement is hereby issued, and all are to comply and not violate it. Sincerely command. Mayor Zhang Qun, concurrently Commander Xiong Shihui."

Shanghai

Postal Workers' Union Clarifies Rumors

Refuting the Ludicrous Theory of the Japanese Newspaper

Solemnly Notifying Members

Recently, the local Postal Workers' Union has been concerned that the Shanghai Japanese newspaper has repeatedly published various inaccurate messages, hoping to incite wind and waves. At this time of social disturbance, the union fears that misunderstandings may arise. Yesterday, it specifically issued a solemn notice to its members, the original text of which is as follows: "Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Notice No. 32, regarding an emergency notice: It has been found that recent messages published in the Japanese newspaper, alleging that postal workers and other workers are planning to engage in improper activities during the May commemorative holidays, are all untrue. The purpose of this union is pure and its actions are prudent. It is extremely attentive to the improvement of workers' treatment, and it also bears a solemn responsibility for the convenience of society and the security of the country. It will never be influenced by external noise or move the actions of this union off the right track. It is hoped that all members will serve faithfully, obey the orders of this union, and not lightly listen to rumors from outside, lest misunderstandings arise. Sincerely issue this notice, April 28th, Republic of China Year 19."

French Concession Cracks Down on Reactionary Propaganda Organization

Located in Bao'an Lane, Xujiahui Road

The General Organization for Reactionary Propaganda

Leaflets Available in Both Chinese and Western Languages

Yesterday morning, Mr. Fevrier, Commissioner of Police of the French Concession, suddenly received a secret report stating that the house at No. 27 Bao'an Lane, Xujiahui Road, was the general headquarters for reactionary propaganda in all of Shanghai. All the printed materials and reactionary leaflets found in Shanghai recently were completely issued from that location. He was requested to investigate quickly. After receiving the report, Mr. Fevrier secretly ordered Political Director Salie to lead Western detectives Sumiano, Mamuya, and Chinese Inspector Cheng Ziqing, Detective Wang Yongkui, Detectives Zhu Liangbi, Fan Guangzhen, Luo Hezhou, Cui Jingyun, Zhou Rongzhang, Wei Yuansheng, and all the detectives of the Political Department, to go to the address by car at approximately 3 PM to search. They seized two large printing presses and various reactionary printed materials on the spot, with content in both Chinese and Western languages. At the same time, five people were arrested and taken to the police station by car for investigation. According to those who know the details, the propaganda organization of the reactionaries has suffered a major blow, and it will be difficult to recover.

New Foreign Affairs Vice Minister Wang Jiazhen Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Scheduled to Arrive in Nanjing Tomorrow

The newly appointed Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang Jiazhen, accompanied by his personal secretary, Guo Yimin, arrived in Shanghai from Dalian yesterday afternoon at 4 PM aboard the Fengtian Maru. After resting briefly in Shanghai, he is scheduled to arrive in Nanjing tomorrow. The details of his arrival and his remarks are described below:

Welcoming Personnel: Those who went to the pier to welcome him yesterday included Zhou Jue, Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Wang Yanxi, Second Secretary of the Embassy in Italy; representatives from the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Gong Debei, Councilor of the Ministry of Internal Affairs; Cen Dezhang, Secretary of the Municipal Government; and Song Ziliang, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Last night, they also visited Wang's residence, the East Asia Hotel.

Arriving in Nanjing Tomorrow: After disembarking, Wang and his entourage immediately took a car to the East Asia Hotel to rest. This reporter made a special visit. Wang was physically robust and very modest in his conversation. According to him, he will rest in Shanghai for one day and arrive in Nanjing on the 30th. When asked about the Russian situation, he replied that what he had heard recently was still going smoothly. If our country wants to recover the China Eastern Railway before the deadline, the cost would be too great. It would be better to negotiate a shortening of the deadline. If negotiations with Russia can be based on the treaty in every aspect, the Russians will naturally have no excuse.

Resting in Liaoning: When asked when Hu Ruoyu would go south to take office as the Minister of Internal Affairs, he said that Hu had been suffering from meningitis in Tianjin and had improved slightly after surgery. He is now recuperating in Liaoning, and there is no definite date for his trip south. He also said that Wu Tiecheng is also in Liaoning. Because he has been running around in various places for many years, he is also willing to take the opportunity to rest temporarily. Therefore, he firmly declined the position of Minister of Internal Affairs.

Wang's Brief Biography: Wang Jiazhen, courtesy name Shuren, is from Shuangcheng, Jilin. In the 13th year of the Republic, he graduated from Keio University in Japan. He immediately served at the Chinese Embassy in Japan for one year. He then went to Hankou. Before long, he became a section chief in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Beijing. He is currently the Director of the Diplomatic Secretariat of the Northeast Border Defense Commander's Office.

Wang Zhengting Arrived in Nanjing Yesterday Afternoon

Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang Zhengting returned to Nanjing by express train at 12:30 PM yesterday afternoon. He told this reporter on the train that he had not yet met with U.S. Ambassador Johnson in Shanghai. Ambassador Johnson is scheduled to go to Nanjing with Italian Ambassador Hualei tonight (last night) to discuss various diplomatic matters. Rumors that Britain and Japan are secretly coordinating and adopting delaying tactics regarding the French rights issue are inaccurate.

Record of the Movements of Prominent Figures

Minister of Railways Sun Ke, Minister of Agriculture and Mining Yi Peiji, and Superintendent of Jianghai Customs Liu Jiwen all took the night train to Beijing last night.

U.S. Minister John N. Johnson is scheduled to take the 11 o'clock night train to Beijing tonight.

Prince Takamatsu, Younger Brother of the Japanese Emperor, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

He Will Rest Quietly on the Ship and Decline Landing

This Morning, He Participates in the Celebration at the Consulate

Prince Takamatsu Nobuhito, the third prince of Emperor Taisho of Japan, was ordered to Europe to reciprocate a visit to the British Emperor. He traveled from Japan with his princess on the Kashima Maru postal ship the day before yesterday. While passing through Shanghai, he stayed for two days at the request of Japanese officials and gentry in Shanghai. At 6:00 AM yesterday, he arrived in Shanghai. More than 150 Japanese officials and gentry residing in Shanghai, including Acting Minister Shigemitsu Aoi, greeted him at the pier. Foreign Minister Wang also sent Director Chen Shiguang to represent the government at the pier to welcome him. However, because the Japanese prince had previously visited Shanghai last year and toured the Shanghai scenery, he decided not to land and tour this time, and declined public and private banquets in order to rest quietly on the ship. Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu had prepared a temporary residence at his private residence on Seymour Road, but the Japanese prince also declined. Today is the Japanese Emperor's birthday, Tencho-setsu. The Japanese prince will land with his princess to attend the remote worship ceremony at the Japanese Consulate. After the ceremony, he will return to the ship to rest. Attached below is a brief biography of the Japanese prince and his entourage:

Brief Biography of the Japanese Prince: Prince Takamatsu Nobuhito is the third prince of Emperor Taisho, born on January 3, 1905. In 1913, he was granted the title of Prince Takamatsu. In 1915, he entered the Gakushuin School. He graduated in March 1920. In May, he entered the Naval Academy. He graduated in July 1924 and was awarded the rank of Ensign. He was assigned to the Asama and Yangtze River warships for practical training. On December 1, 1925, he was officially commissioned as a Navy Ensign, awarded the Grand Cordon of the Supreme Order of the Chrysanthemum, and trained on the warship Fuso. In 1926, he graduated from the Naval Torpedo School and the Artillery School. In 1926, he was promoted to Lieutenant in the Navy and assigned to the warship Yakumo, dispatched to visit various ports in the South Seas and the naval authorities of various countries. In September 1929, he was appointed to the Naval General Staff Office. He married on February 4th of this year and traveled abroad.

Entourage: Navy Lieutenant Commander Takeo Yamagata, Iwakichi Ishikawa, Taisuke Mizuno, Doctor of Medicine Tsuneo Sakamoto, attendants and maids Ochiai, Kuroda, Shibu, Yamamoto.

Japanese Consulate Celebrates Tencho-setsu Today

Today is the Emperor of Japan's birthday, Tencho-setsu. Japanese officials and gentry are preparing for the celebration with great enthusiasm. The Japanese Consulate, acting as the embassy, is hosting guests from China and abroad to receive congratulations. In advance, Acting Minister Shigemitsu Aoi sent out invitations. The celebration ceremony will be held at the consulate at 9:30 AM. Prince Takamatsu and the princess will also attend. At the same time, guests from China and abroad will be invited to a remote worship ceremony at 10:30 AM, and the meeting will end at 11:00 AM. In the afternoon, a celebration ceremony and entertainment will be held at the New Park. The army, navy, and Japanese volunteer corps, and male and female students from various schools will hold a military parade. In the evening, there will be a lantern parade. Japanese banks, stores, schools, and public offices will all be closed for the day and fly flags to celebrate.

Population Statistics Report of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau

The Municipal Public Safety Bureau compiles monthly statistics on population changes within the city. According to the bureau's report for last month, the number of households in each district of the city is 185,084 registered households and 160,272 attached households. The population consists of 939,712 males and 695,114 females. There are 2,004 registered and attached foreign households, with a total population of 9,463 males and females. The special districts still follow the old statistics of 1,158,355 Chinese and 40,324 foreigners. Adding these figures together, the total population of the city is 2,842,968, an increase of 20,699 in population compared to February.

Public Buses Have No Hope of Resuming Service in the Short Term

Negotiations Between the Two Sides Have Stalled

The strike of public bus workers in the Public Concession has lasted for ten days. Negotiations between the strike representatives and the company regarding the conditions for resuming work are still stalled. According to Mr. Peng Na, a clerk of the company, the crux of the stalemate is that the workers are demanding that wages be paid as usual during the strike period, which the company cannot accept. As a result, the negotiations have reached a deadlock. There is no certainty as to when the workers will resume work. However, the company is currently training Russians and hopes to resume the first public bus route soon. The first route was originally from Jing'an Temple to Hongkou Park, but it has now been temporarily shortened to Jing'an Temple to Waibaidu Bridge.

According to the Da Wan Bao, this morning (28th), news from the police indicates that public buses in the Public Concession are unlikely to resume service within the current week. This is because company officials fear that if service resumes before May 1st, the vehicles will be attacked. Therefore, they have decided to wait until the end of the week to observe the situation before announcing the resumption date. The Russians who have been hired are still undergoing training, and they are scheduled to go to the Public Works Department's Transportation Bureau today and tomorrow to take the examination for a license.

No Results from Negotiations in the Public Concession Tram Workers' Strike

News from the Union: The Public Tram Strike Committee sent three representatives to negotiate with the management yesterday. After the three representatives met with the company's manager, the manager not only completely rejected the workers' conditions, but also said that the workers' representatives were too young and not qualified, and that the number of people was too small to be considered representatives. In addition, he led one of the three representatives into the room and said, "You three are not qualified to be representatives. I will now designate the following numbers as representatives. You can go find them to negotiate." He then wrote down several numbers and left the room. The representatives believed that the management was not sincere in negotiating and left in disappointment. After the Strike Committee received the report from the three representatives, it felt that it was unheard of for the management to designate negotiation representatives and believed that the management was deliberately undermining worker solidarity and plotting to sabotage the strike. It was greatly angered and immediately issued an emergency flyer to all workers, announcing that the management was using divisive tactics to sabotage the strike conspiracy, and called on all workers to adhere to strike discipline, absolutely obey the orders of the Strike Committee, and act in unison. All workers were very angry when they heard the news and decided that if any individual acted alone without the order of the Strike Committee, they would be considered a scab and a traitor and would be dealt with severely according to strike discipline.

News from the Company: Yesterday, three representatives from the workers went to the Tram Company on Suzhou Road to negotiate the conditions, but there were no results. Mr. Bao Qishi, the general manager of the Tram Company, told reporters yesterday, "Recently, three representatives came to the company to negotiate the conditions, but these three were not tram workers, and I do not recognize their qualifications as representatives, so negotiations did not begin. However, the company is very willing to be close to the workers. If the workers send formal representatives, I am very willing to negotiate with them sincerely. It is expected that tomorrow (that is, today), the workers will have formal representatives to come here to discuss."

German Industrial Delegation Travels to Hangzhou Yesterday

The German industrial delegation led by Mr. Paoziman and others have been in Shanghai for several days. Due to the large number of social engagements, they took the 9:00 AM express train to Hangzhou yesterday morning for sightseeing. The Zhejiang Provincial Government sent a special representative to receive them. The delegation will stay in Hangzhou for about one or two days before returning to Shanghai and taking a ship to Tianjin by sea.

Japanese Naval Group Arrives in Shanghai

In response to the situation in China, the Japanese Ministry of the Navy has increased the strength of its Yangtze River naval forces. It has specially dispatched a small team of naval soldiers from Sasebo, including Oda, Kimura, and Tanaka Shinichi, to China. They arrived in Shanghai by ship yesterday. They did not stay in Shanghai but immediately transferred to Nanjing to serve on the Beijing-based warship Saga, ready to land to protect Japanese nationals if necessary.

Dredging Bureau Dredges Suzhou Creek

Since taking office, Song Ziliang, the director of the Dredging Bureau, has been working hard to rectify the bureau's affairs. Recognizing that the silting of the lower reaches of Suzhou Creek (from Waibaidu Bridge to Yejidun) is closely related to the Huangpu River, he proposed a dredging plan at the bureau's meeting. Later, because the creek is under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Special Municipality, he obtained the consent of Mayor Zhang and was determined to proceed. He specially invited other bureau directors and representatives from the Municipal Government, as well as Port Director Xi Dingmo, to board a small boat and survey the creek section by section, according to the map, in order to start construction. The previous report that he requested financial assistance from the Public Works Department and invited Public Works Department Director Kangding to inspect the area together is not true; there is no such person. It is also heard that the Construction Committee is now proposing a dredging plan, which is likely related to the entire creek project and will be implemented.
