Local News

Special District Court Heavily Guarded, More Than One Hundred Youths Escorted to the Municipal Public Safety Bureau

Among the 107 people, there were seven women. Only Tang Xicheng was bailed out by the Japanese Cotton Mill.

Details of the Disturbance the Previous Morning: At 10:00 AM the previous morning, several hundred youths suddenly gathered near the Dongxin Bridge on Zhejiang Road in the Public Concession. Although they were dispersed by detectives, at 10:45 AM, the crowd poured into Renji Shantang at 566 Yunnan Road, intending to hold a meeting. Later, the police authorities urgently dispatched Chinese and Western constables from the reserve team of the Gordon Road Police Station, together with the Tongban detectives from the Laozha Police Station, to surround Renji Shantang. They then entered the building to stop the meeting and arrested as many as 107 men and women at the scene. The rest scattered. At the time, the order at the scene was somewhat chaotic, but fortunately the authorities coordinated well and order was quickly restored.

Seven Young Women: Among the 107 people arrested, there were seven young women. According to the names they provided at the police station, they were Wang Chunhua, Chen Fengzhen, Zhao Min, Lin Shuzhi, Jiang Tao, Jiang Bo, and Lin Xiuying.

List of Names of One Hundred Men: In addition, the names of the one hundred men are as follows: Lü Fu, Zhang Fuxiang, Li Mei, Shen Jingen, Li Biancheng, Tang Xicheng, Wang Dingxun, Liu Wenzhi, Wu Guohua, Chen Kangbai, Ye Jinkang, Zhou Zhongzuo, Zhou Xingran, Chen Bingsheng, Jin Qin Yu, Xiao Dalang, Chen Afeng, Zhu Xuansen, Wu Gaozi, Zhou Xiang, Ni Shengfa, Wan Zhikui, Huang Abao, Li Xinfa, Wu Mei, Xu Zhiwen, Zhou Jijie, Huang Lizhi, Li Xisheng, Wang Ren, Fang Weiqin, Hou Gaosheng, Wang Jinxiang, Cao Zhengben, Chen Sixiao, Lin Youying, Wang Agen, Cai Si, Jin Wenbao, Li Jinxiang, Wang Jinfu, Feng Shanlin, Feng Rujue, Kong Xisheng, Xu Zhongnian, Zheng Diqun, Huang Daji, Zhong Hanji, Wang Baode, Li Jinsheng, Li Fugeng, Dong Zhengshi, Wang Zhende, Cao Fusheng, Zhu Yeguang, Wang Caikuan, Zhang Baoxiang, Li Xiaosan, Hu Bangwen, Chen Asi, Shi Agou, Feng Changan, Wu Kaiguo, Cao Ruguan, Ma Yiming, Chen Zhi, Hong Qingquan, Xiang Qishun, Cao Fusi, Feng Xizhai, Cao Adong, Qiu Weijia, Yi Zhiren, Pan Dekuan, Ying Shiyuan, Zhu A'er, Ma Qichang, Chen Song, Cao A Jin, Li Linbao, Shui Qinghua, Tao Azhong, Wang Jianzhi, Cao A Hai, Guan Xiaodongzi, Yang A Er, Zhang Jinwu, Shi Jianheng, Chen Rongsheng, Li Xiaosi, Chang Afu, Zhang Guojun, Wang Ren, Duan Xueqing, Jiang Yushu, Feng Masi, Yang Kelin, Chen Mingxiang, Luo Xingde, Chen Yinghua.

No Such Large Detention Center: At the time, a large number of various reactionary banners were seized and taken to the Laozha Police Station. The police chief ordered the seven women to be transferred to the women's prison of the Special District Local Court for detention. The one hundred men were divided between the General Patrol Station and the Xinzha Patrol Station to avoid overcrowding because the police station did not have such a large detention center.

The Court is Heavily Guarded: At 10:00 AM yesterday, Judge Du Fuyao of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court specially opened the First Criminal Court for a preliminary hearing. When they were escorted from the police station to the court, armed Chinese and Western constables were dispatched to protect them along the way. After arriving at the court, the armed constables were stationed at the entrance of the court, and the security was very strict.

The Interrogation Took a Long Time: Judge Du took his seat, and all 107 people were brought into the courtroom. Observing their ages, they were all in their early twenties and were students and workers. Judge Du then questioned them one by one, asking their age, hometown, address, etc. By noon, only half of them had been questioned, so he temporarily adjourned the court for lunch and a brief rest, and then resumed his seat at about 2:00 PM to continue the proceedings and question them one by one. Only Wang Ren and Li Xiaosi changed their names. Wang claimed that his real name was Zhao Tailai, and Li claimed that his original name was Su Hanping.

Transfer by the Municipal Public Safety Bureau: Subsequently, a detective from the Municipal Public Safety Bureau presented a document requesting permission to transfer them to the Municipal Public Safety Bureau for interrogation.

Many Iron Bars and Lime: Bogliang Rubao Yi, the lawyer of the police station, also stated the circumstances of the case, saying that the defendants suddenly went to Renji Shantang on Yunnan Road yesterday morning, hoping to hold a meeting. The hall usually provides diagnosis and medication. Although it was a Sunday yesterday and there were no consultations, the door was not closed, so they were able to enter. When the police received the report, they dispatched detectives. Upon entering the building, they first discovered many iron bars and lime bags. These two items were prepared by them, perhaps to injure others.

The Police Received a Tip-off in Advance: In addition, many leaflets were seized, all of which contained counter-revolutionary content. The police station received a report from the Public Safety Bureau in advance, so they stepped up their precautions. After investigating, it was found that none of the people arrested were residents of the concession. The Public Safety Bureau requested a transfer, and the police station did not object.

Tang Xicheng May Be Exempt from Prosecution: However, Tang Xicheng, one of the people arrested, is an employee of a Japanese cotton mill. Yesterday, the factory sent people to inquire about the news and was arrested along with the others. Now the Japanese employer has arrived at the court, and after he proves his identity, the police station can withdraw the charges against Tang.

The Western Constable Reported Everything: Constable No. 169 also reported the situation at the time, saying, "At about 8:00 AM yesterday morning, I was patrolling outside in a car and saw many male and female students walking in groups along Dongxin Bridge. At 10:40 AM, extending to Yunnan Road, I saw a large number of students wanting to go to Renji Hall to hold a meeting. I immediately went to investigate and saw that the courtyard inside the building was already crowded with people. Some people were holding flags, others were distributing leaflets, and one person was giving a speech. When they saw me, one of the students threw a bag of lime at me. I immediately arrested him. There was also a basket full of glass bottles in the room."

Statement of Head Constable Feng: According to the report of Chinese head constable Feng Ruisheng, he first saw male and female students gathering at Dongxin Bridge and dispersed them, but they soon reunited. Later, he suddenly lost sight of them, and later learned that they had gone to Renji Hall to hold a meeting. He also rushed there and saw two red flags hanging outside the gate of the hall, so he returned to the police station and summoned detectives to stop them.

Tang Xicheng is Granted Release: Finally, Mr. Ganggan, a Japanese national from the Nei Wai Cotton Mill, proved that Tang Xicheng was sent by the factory to gather information and was not a reactionary. Judge Du concluded the preliminary hearing and announced that Tang Xicheng was granted bail.

The Men and Women Were Transferred Together: The remaining 106 men and women were allowed to be taken back by the officials from the Municipal Public Safety Bureau for interrogation. At that time, the temporary police inside and outside the court also withdrew.

Thugs at the Intersection of Caishi Road Reiterate the May 30th Massacre

Claiming to be Bringing Glory to the Country

Because the Gu Zhenghong Case Was Handled

There Was No Riotous Behavior This Time

Fifteen People Were Tried and Awaiting Further Interrogation

On the 16th of last month, hundreds of young men and women gathered at the intersection of Caishi Road and Kangti Road in the French Concession, shouting slogans against imperialism, holding flags, and throwing stones at trolleybuses. When the police learned of this, they immediately ordered detectives to rush to the scene to disperse them. They arrested Chu Zhixiang, Liu Jizhao, Song Zhongjie, Xie Yunju, Guo Deming, Lü Juefan, Li Yushu, Bao Susheng, Li Guangyuan, Luo Zhong, Li Yuebai, Huang Shoutian, Dong Bixong, Han Weiyi, and the woman Zhou Wenjun, and seized a red cloth flag with the Western code "CP" written on it, as well as dozens of stones. They were all taken to the police station and, after being interrogated in the French Court, the defendants denied everything and were ordered to await further investigation. Yesterday, they were interrogated again. First, Western Detective Sarge stated that the statements made by the defendants in the court last time were not true. Now, the police station has found that the defendants have no fixed addresses, which shows that they are troublemakers. Please investigate. When asked, Chu Zhixiang confessed that he had been detained and tried in court in the Public Concession during the May 30th Massacre because he represented the workers who were massacred in the Gu Zhenghong incident. This was bringing glory to the country and was a legitimate matter. Although they had passed through the area this time, they had not engaged in any riotous behavior and were indeed mistakenly arrested. The rest of the defendants gave similar answers. Chinese and Western officials ordered them to be remanded in custody to await sentencing.

Two More People Accused of Counter-Revolutionary Crimes

Border Cannons Hidden in Kerosene Tanks

Each Also Carried Reactionary Leaflets

The day before yesterday, police stations in the Public Concession stepped up precautions in their respective jurisdictions and were particularly strict with inspections. Therefore, in addition to arresting a large number of men and women at Renji Shantang, there were two other cases of arrests along the way. One was at 9:15 AM when Bao Tan Liu Chunshu and Huang Fusen of the Laozha Police Station were searching near the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Beihai Road. They saw a Jiangxi man named Li Jincai carrying a kerosene tank. They searched it and found many border cannons. He had a bundle of reactionary leaflets hidden on his person. There was also a piece of white paper listing the names of five people, so they arrested him and seized two small red and white flags in the alley. The other was near Gordon Road and Roberts Road. At the same time, Bao Tan Kong Qingping of the Putuo Road Police Station and Chinese and Japanese constables were searching pedestrians when they saw a Zhejiang man named Hu Xiangmu coming from the front, holding a paper box. They opened the box and inspected it, and it was full of reactionary leaflets, so they took him to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were both sent to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Both were prosecuted for counter-revolutionary acts. Judge Du Fuyao specially opened the First Criminal Court for a preliminary hearing. First, court lawyer Ru Bao Yi stated the facts of the case, saying that border cannons were certainly fired by these people at the beginning of their actions as a signal. After Judge Du briefly questioned the two defendants about their age and origin, he ordered them to be taken into custody for further interrogation at a later date.

People Distributing Reactionary Leaflets Also Found in Pudong

One Ma Desheng

Two Elementary School Students

Ma Desheng, from Wuhu, was walking near the Shenyuli of the Taoyuanzhai Garden Stone Bridge in Pudong at about 9:00 PM the night before last when many reactionary leaflets were suddenly found on the ground. The patrol police of the Third District Public Safety Bureau believed that Ma was walking in a hurry and was not a good person, so they stepped forward to arrest him and take him to the district. Yesterday, after the district chief interrogated Ma, Ma confessed that he was 42 years old and lived at No. 12 Yanchang Road, Pudong.

He worked as a dock coolie at Yilongmao Pier and had previously served as a platoon leader in the Huangpu Training Corps. He followed Commander-in-Chief Jiang from Shaoguan and went through Hunan, Hubei, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi. Later, he asked for a long leave due to illness and came to Shanghai, resulting in unemployment, so he became a coolie. He did not distribute reactionary leaflets. The authorities believed that Ma's confession was not credible and ordered a written order to escort him to the Public Safety Bureau for disposition.

At 8:00 AM yesterday morning, a child named Wang Linhe, 11 years old, was found carrying 40 reactionary leaflets while walking near Sanwanchang, Lujiazui, Pudong. He was discovered by the post police of the Fourth Squadron and the child and the leaflets were sent to the Third District. After Wang was interrogated, he stated that the leaflets were brought by Zhang Gengsheng, an elementary school student from the Chen School next door, and told him to take them to his uncle's house, which led to their discovery. Then Zhang Gengsheng was summoned and confessed that he was 14 years old, a local, and lived behind the Wu family. The leaflets were given to him by someone wearing a gray cloth long gown and asked him to distribute them. He then handed them to Wang Linhe and did not know that they were reactionary propaganda items. It was ordered that the two children Wang and Zhang, along with the leaflets, be sent to the General Bureau for investigation.

A Bizarre Case: Instigating Husband's Murder and Surrendering

Husband and Wife Had Been Very Affectionate

Vehemently Denying Conspiracy to Murder Her Husband

The Informant Speaks with Certainty

Waiting for Shen Honggao to be Summoned for Further Inquiry

Ni, the wife of Shen Hongchuan from Tongzhou, along with Zhang Yuqing and Xu Qingyun, were apprehended yesterday by the Mixed Court police and brought before the Shanghai Special District Local Court, accused of conspiring to murder Shen Hongchuan. Judge Wu Tingqi conducted a preliminary hearing. According to the police lawyer, yesterday afternoon (the 27th), Chen Yulin reported to the Mixed Court police that on April 6th, Zhang Yuqing and Xu Qingyun, residing at No. 1425 North Shanxi Road, went together to a small teahouse near the Tangjia Lane vegetable market. They told him that Shen Ni was asking him to murder her husband Shen Hongchuan because he was excessively extravagant and addicted to opium. They arranged to meet again in seven days at a teahouse near the Old Zha Gate Bridge to discuss the matter further. At the appointed time, he met with the woman and Zhang and Xu at the agreed-upon location. Zhang and Xu gave him eight silver dollars, twelve small silver coins, and a colored scarf. Later, he couldn't bring himself to commit such a heinous act, so he informed Shen Hongchuan. However, Shen refused to believe him, so he reported the matter, etc. At the time, Chen handed over the silver dollars and the scarf to the police. Therefore, the police sent detectives to arrest Shen Ni, Zhang, and Xu. Because the informant was a key witness, he was also temporarily detained. Now, her husband, Shen Hongchuan, has been summoned, requesting an inquiry, etc. Shen Hongchuan testified that he is 33 years old and runs a kiln goods shop in Shanghai. Ni is his legal wife, and they have been married for eleven years, with three sons and two daughters. The relationship between husband and wife has always been harmonious, and his wife's character is excellent. There is no way she would have such malicious intentions. Chen Yulin used to be a cohabitant, so they knew each other. A few days ago, Chen suddenly told him that his wife wanted to murder him and urged him to sell his wife quickly. He did not heed his words. Later, Chen borrowed fifteen dollars from him, which he also refused. He then went to the police to fabricate a false accusation, hoping to frame him, requesting a strict investigation, etc. Chen Yulin testified that the reported facts were true, and if there were any falsehoods, he was willing to accept severe punishment, etc. Shen Li, Shen Hongchuan's mother, testified that her son, Hongchuan, and his daughter-in-law, Ni, were usually very harmonious. It can be asserted that Ni would never have any intention of murdering her husband and is actually being framed, etc. Shen Ni, in addition to vehemently denying any conspiracy to murder her husband, also stated that her husband's elder brother, Shen Honggao, previously had a dispute with her husband over inheritance and was involved in a lawsuit in their hometown of Tongzhou. Since then, the brothers have been at odds, and Honggao has always harbored intentions to harm her and her husband. She asked for a clear investigation into the reason, etc. The police lawyer requested that Shen Honggao also be summoned as a key witness in the case to clarify the truth. Judge Wu ordered that the three defendants, Shen Ni, etc., and the witness Chen Yulin, be detained separately and wait for another hearing on a different date.

Husband in Jail, Wife Having an Affair at Home

It Can Be Said She Is Heartless

The Father-in-law Gathered People to Catch Them

Chen Xingshan, a 54-year-old farmer from Zhujia Bang, Gonghe Xin Road, Zhabei, has a son named Chen Liugen, who used to be a road worker. Therefore, she formed an inseparable bond with Wang Wenbing, a fellow worker from Huzhou, and openly had adulterous relations with Wang Wenbing at home, as if they were husband and wife. However, the good times did not last long, and her father-in-law, Chen Xingshan, found out. Extortionists Arrange to Collect Money in the Park

The Extortionist Arrived on a Bicycle

Detectives Swarmed Forward and Arrested Him

He then took a tram back to Zhu's house. When the tram arrived at the New World stop, and he was walking along Guling Road, a person suddenly asked Luo if he was Zhu's representative. Luo said yes. The person then asked if he had brought the money. Luo immediately told him that Zhu's finances were exhausted, but he could barely raise a few hundred dollars. The person said that at least five hundred dollars was needed and arranged to deliver it at 10 a.m. on the 26th at the China Park on Sichuan Road Bridge. Luo then reported to the police station. Detectives Ruan Yao, Bao Tan Ma Jiayong, etc., rushed to the location the next morning and ambushed near the park. Luo waited at the arranged place. Soon, the extortionist who had made the arrangement with Luo arrived on a bicycle and asked if the money was ready. Luo told him that only two hundred dollars had been prepared. The detectives swarmed out and arrested the extortionist along with his bicycle. Upon questioning, he revealed his name as Zhang Quansheng, from Jiangbei, who works as a rickshaw puller in Shanghai. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Shanghai Special District Local Court, where Judge Wu conducted a preliminary hearing. Luo and Zhu successively explained the situation. The defendant confessed that someone else had initiated the matter and that person had already escaped. He was being fooled, etc. The court ordered the defendant to be detained, and the hearing was adjourned for further investigation.

Wang Along Died Tragically

Woman Accuses Husband of Neglecting Support

Defendant Replies That There Is No Relationship

Claims Plaintiff Is Forcing Herself to Be His Wife

Gao Feng, a 41-year-old local woman, accompanied by her son, Gao Xiangsheng, 20 years old, went to the Shanghai Local Court to accuse her husband, Gao Songlin, of abandoning his legal wife and neglecting support, requesting to live together, etc. Her statement stated that when the plaintiff was 21 years old, Gu Ren and Wu A'er served as matchmakers. Gao Songlin was looking for a wife because his previous wife had passed away and he lacked someone to take care of the household. Therefore, the plaintiff married the defendant. For the first few years, they lived peacefully. The following year, she gave birth to a son named Xiangsheng (the second plaintiff), who is now 20 years old. The defendant used to run a southern goods store in Caojiadu. He then discussed with the plaintiff, asking the plaintiff to live separately. The plaintiff initially did not think much of it. In recent years, the defendant has not returned home and has neglected the livelihood of the plaintiff and her son. The plaintiff repeatedly argued with him, and although the defendant admitted his fault, he still did not provide any support. The plaintiff could initially make a living by working, but because of old age and illness, she cannot support herself. The defendant heartlessly abandoned his legal wife, failing as a husband. She requested that the defendant be summoned to court and ordered to live with the plaintiff, etc. The defendant, Gao Songlin, stated that he has no physical relationship with the woman and was surprised by the unfounded lawsuit. He hired lawyer Wei Wenhan to file a response, arguing that the plaintiff was misrepresenting the facts and making false accusations, requesting dismissal. The defendant is 55 years old. He has been able to console himself throughout his life that his legal wife is still alive and well. Relatives and neighbors are all aware of this. His younger brother, Gao Qilin, and Chen Hongshan, a tenant who has lived with him for over 20 years, can all testify. Now, unfortunately, the harmonious couple has been cursed by others, who strongly wish for the defendant's wife to be deceased. The plaintiff and her son are making claims with no basis to force themselves as his wife and son. It is outrageous. The defendant and the plaintiff were only neighbors and had met a few times. Later, the plaintiff moved away. After many years, she ran out of options and tried to borrow money from the defendant, citing their former neighborly relationship. He refused, and she shamelessly tried to force herself as his wife. There is no limit to her madness. The plaintiff and the defendant have no marital relationship. The so-called abandonment and neglect of support are completely irrelevant. He requested that the lawsuit be dismissed, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Du held a court hearing. The plaintiffs, Gao Feng and Gao Xiangsheng, recounted the previous events. The defendant, Gao Songlin, denied that the plaintiff was his wife. The witnesses Gao Lin and Chen Hongshan testified that the defendant still has a legal wife at home. After receiving the testimony, the judge ordered the defendant to bring his legal wife to court for verification at the next hearing. The court was then adjourned.

Pitiful Fate of a Young Widow

Becoming a Young Widow and Coming to Shanghai to Work

Found by Her Father-in-Law, She Painfully Returns Home

Wei Lü, a young woman of 18 years old, from Xinchang County, Zhejiang Province, was betrothed to her cousin, Wei Qingjiang, by her mother, Lü Wei, since childhood. They married in November of last year, and the relationship between husband and wife was very close. However, just one month after the marriage, Wei Qingjiang suddenly fell seriously ill and died. Lü, in her prime, suddenly became a widow, feeling very sad. Her in-laws not only did not show any sympathy but blamed her for her son's death, saying that Lü's fate was not good. They often abused her. Lü could not bear it. Before seven weeks, she seized the opportunity to escape back to her mother's house. With the help of a relative named Wang, she came to Shanghai and worked as a female worker at the Yong'an Second Cotton Mill in Wusong Yunzao Bang, residing in the factory's No. 10 workshop. After Lü ran away, her father-in-law, Wei Baosheng (also her maternal uncle), immediately inquired about Lü's whereabouts from his sister, Lü Wei. Lü Wei feigned ignorance. Wei Baosheng then sent people to investigate everywhere. He soon found out that Lü was now in Wusong. He immediately came to Shanghai from his hometown. Yesterday morning at 11 a.m., he took a car to Wusong and went to the Yong'an No. 10 workshop, where he found Lü. Lü suddenly saw her father-in-law and took the opportunity to run away, trying to hide. However, she was caught halfway. Lü wailed and cried, firmly unwilling to return to Xinchang with her father-in-law. For a time, onlookers gathered. Officer Shi of the Seventh District First Branch of the Public Security Bureau was patrolling and passed by. After inquiring about the situation, he felt that Wei Lü's fate was pitiful, but living alone in a foreign land was not a long-term solution. He persuaded both Wei Lü and Wei Baosheng. Lü finally agreed to return to her hometown with her father-in-law. Wei Baosheng also agreed to take Lü back to Xinchang and hand her over to his sister, Lü Wei. The father-in-law and daughter-in-law then took the train to Shanghai.

Convenience of Visiting Sheshan

Special Ship Prepared at Xinzhuang

Sheshan, a scenic spot belonging to Songjiang County, has long been famous. Every spring, visitors flock there. However, in the past, due to inconvenient transportation, travel was quite troublesome. Therefore, those who lived in relatively remote areas were deterred, only longing for it in their hearts. It is heard that the Xinzhuang Tongli Navigation Company, to facilitate those visiting Sheshan, will launch special steamship services starting from May 1st. Visitors can take the 7 a.m. express train from Shanghai to Xinzhuang, then transfer to a steamship directly to Sheshan. At 4 p.m., the ship returns to Xinzhuang to connect with the 8:37 train to Shanghai. The fare is four dimes per person, and the meal fee is two dimes per person. Visitors who wish to stay overnight can stay in the dormitory. The accommodation fee is two dimes per person. The time is approaching for the welcoming of the Holy Mother. With convenient transportation, it is expected that Catholics and visitors from all over will be even more crowded than before.

A Man and a Woman Suddenly Enter Yihe Cotton Mill

Accused of Inciting a Strike

Sentenced to Three Days Detention

At 6 p.m. on the night before last, as the night shift at the Yihe Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road was starting, Guan Runhong from Changzhou and Xu Xiaomei, a woman from Anhui, suddenly entered the mill and were active there. Soldier Crushed to Death by Train

Returning to His Hometown of Ruian County on Leave

Jumping off the Train in Haste, He Died Tragically

Yesterday morning around 9 a.m., a third- and fourth-class passenger train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, heading from Shanghai to Wuxi, ran over a soldier near the Gujiazai area near the Zhenru station. The deceased was wearing a gray uniform and was lying face down on the ground to the right of the railway, with his head to the east and his feet to the west. His left foot was crushed. The location was about five or six li north of Gujiazai and east of the station. He also had a paper long leave pass, two pay slips, two silver dollars, and two dimes. Considering the cause of death, it is likely that he boarded the wrong train and jumped off in haste, resulting in his injury and death.

The Truth About the Arrest of Crew Members of the Taisun Ship

A Major Tragedy of Stevedore Brawls

The Taisun, a vessel of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, recently traveled from Shanghai to Wenzhou. Upon arrival, significant incidents occurred, including the arrest of crew members over alleged rice theft and a fatal brawl among dockworkers. Now that the ship has returned to Shanghai, the full details of these events have been investigated and are recorded below.

Traveler’s Smoking Set Causes Trouble for Crew

Recently, Wenzhou has been strictly enforcing local defense measures, especially with the organization of a joint military-police inspection bureau. All merchant ships arriving at the port are subject to thorough passenger inspections. This time, when the Taisun ship arrived in Wenzhou, before it had even docked, the military-police inspection bureau dispatched twenty soldiers, led by a platoon leader, on small sampans to board the ship from the stern. They spread out to inspect all the cabins. In the steerage compartment (leased to passengers), a complete smoking set was discovered. Four soldiers from the inspection team confiscated the contraband and demanded that the crew hand over the person carrying it. Amidst the commotion, the passenger had already escaped. The crew searched without success, but the soldiers insisted, dragging Second Purser Wang from the Second Purser’s office. While waiting, the ship's accountant, Wang Lanqing, and the steward, Jian Rong, arrived and explained to the soldiers that the passenger smuggling the contraband could not be found. The four soldiers then produced hemp ropes and tied up Wang and Jian, taking them away. At the time, Wang and Jian were only in their underwear and barefoot, not even having time to put on clothes. They were detained at the inspection bureau. Crew members who went to bail them out that night were refused, being told that only the surrender of the actual culprit would secure their release. Therefore, when the Taisun returned to Shanghai yesterday from Wenzhou, Wang and Jian had not yet been released. The matter has now been reported to the bureau's business director for intervention.

Stealing Rice by Warehouse Clerk Leads to Major Conflict

Due to famine in Wenzhou, large quantities of foreign rice were procured in Shanghai for price stabilization. The Taisun also transported this rice to Wenzhou. The crew took the transportation of the rice very seriously, as they would have to compensate for any shortages. Therefore, they were extremely cautious during unloading. Among the rice being unloaded, there was a batch purchased by the Yongli Warehouse. During unloading, the crew discovered that a clerk from the warehouse was stealing rice. He was caught and reported to the dock police, who arrested him. Unexpectedly, this sparked a major conflict. The arrested clerk was forcibly retrieved by people from the rice warehouse. A brawl ensued with the police. Furthermore, the rice warehouse side held a public meeting, denying any theft and claiming that the crew had slandered their reputation. They demanded that the Taisun ship compensate for the losses, with the following conditions: (1) a penalty of thirty tables of wine, (2) two opera performances, and (3) an apology. Eventually, through the mediation of the public association, the Taisun ship was persuaded to settle the matter peacefully by admitting to a fine of two tables of wine and paying for firecrackers. The incident was thus resolved.

Dockworkers Fighting Over Cargo Results in Four Deaths

Dockworkers in Wenzhou are divided into different gangs. Among the stevedores, there are so-called "Seafarers' Gang" and "Firewood Gang." Those working at the China Merchants Bureau dock belong to the Seafarers' Gang. This time, when the Taisun arrived in Wenzhou, workers from various gangs competed to unload the cargo. The Firewood Gang workers and the Seafarers' Gang workers fought over the cargo, leading to a brawl. This matter was unrelated to the ship and not something the shipping bureau should interfere with, so no intervention was made. The two gangs engaged in a major fight on the dock, using poles and other weapons to strike each other. As a result, four workers from the Firewood Gang died from their severe injuries. The local public security bureau has arrested all the workers involved in the violence. This tragic incident has led to significant complications.

Wenzhou Ships to Shanghai Are All Delayed

Since the fatal brawl among the dockworkers, dockworkers have gone on strike, ceasing to load and unload cargo. The China Merchants Bureau has three ships in Wenzhou. Apart from the Guangli, which sailed to Shanghai first, the Taisun's arrival in Shanghai was also delayed due to the temporary work stoppage, which delayed its cargo loading. Furthermore, the Guangji, which was supposed to arrive in Shanghai yesterday, will now be delayed by one day and is scheduled to arrive today.

The Red Cross Society Held Re-elections Yesterday

Waiting for the National Government to Send Personnel to Supervise the Unsealing

The Third General Meeting of Members of the Chinese Red Cross Society, following the resolution of the General Meeting, organized a preparatory re-election committee. The situation has been reported previously. Yesterday morning, after the memorial week, Chairman Wang Yiting reported on the findings of the preparatory re-election committee, and Committee Member Wang Yiting presented re-election proposals. The proposals were seconded by committee members Huang Hanzhi, Wu Wei, and Guan Gangzhi. Supplementary opinions were offered by Qingpu representative Xu Xichun, Lü County representative Dong Lin, and re-election committee members Gu Keyong and Shen Laisen. Before a vote could be taken, lunch was served. The meeting continued at 2:00 PM, with Wen Lanting attending and announcing his views, which were unanimously endorsed. Voting commenced immediately. The number of delegates present accounted for more than three-quarters of the total registered. As the National Government and the Party Department had not yet sent personnel to supervise, it was decided to seal the ballot boxes on the spot. The ballot counters Wang Peiyuan, Zhou Guoxun, Dong Lin, and Zhou Guangji handed them over to the chairman, Wang Yiting, for safekeeping, pending the arrival of National Government personnel to supervise the unsealing, to ensure utmost caution.

The Silk Cocoon Merchants' Association Convened a Meeting of Cocoon Merchants

The General Association of Silk Cocoon Merchants of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui convened a temporary discussion meeting of silk cocoon merchants at 3:00 PM yesterday (the 28th). Over ninety people attended, including Shen Moushen, Zhu Jing'an, and Wu Shenbo. Huang Moushen chaired the meeting. After announcing the purpose of the meeting, the first item discussed was the issue of foreign firms not complying with the resolution regarding the weight and quality of silk delivered by the merchants. Several merchants rose to report that since the implementation of standardized public weighing on April 1st, factories have switched to using canvas bags and eliminated oil slips, white paper, and hemp bags. However, foreign firms still demand oil paper and hemp bags, as well as extracting sample silk strands for testing. It was previously resolved that two strands should be drawn from every five bundles, and the foreign firms should issue receipts and return them after weighing. The Export Silk Association had agreed to comply with this resolution. However, apart from firms such as Huatong, Weicheng, Hulin, and Jingxing, the others still extract one strand from each bundle and do not issue receipts or specify the weight of the strands. The Mitsui firm is the worst offender, not only extracting more strands but even refusing to load the silk onto ships unless oil paper and hemp bags are provided, violating the resolution. The merchants felt it was difficult to deliver silk due to these extra demands. It was resolved unanimously to reject the demands and to instruct brokers to firmly refuse them. A letter was also sent to the Export Silk Association, requesting that it immediately inform all foreign firms to cease these extra demands to maintain good relations. The next item discussed was the increase in discounts for cocoon loan insurance premiums. The delegates who attended the Sino-foreign joint meeting, Shen Moushen and Wu Shenbo, reported on the situation at the meeting of the foreign insurance association. It was resolved that the association would convene a general meeting this week and respond after the meeting. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

The First Publicity Meeting of the Municipal Publicity Department

The Publicity Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee convened its first municipal publicity meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon. The meeting was chaired by Chen Dezheng, the head of the Municipal Publicity Department. After opening the meeting with formal ceremonies, the chairman gave a report. Then, the following items were discussed: (1) How to prevent reactionary elements from using the May Revolution Commemoration to hold gatherings. (Resolution) Handle in accordance with the central government's secret order. (2) How to construct revolutionary literature for propaganda in addition to strictly investigating and prohibiting the proliferation of reactionary literary publications on the market. (Resolution) (1) Party publications in each district of this city should publish as much revolutionary literary theory and creation as possible. (2) Submit a revolutionary literary publication edited by the Municipal Publicity Department. (3) Each district should separately organize a May Revolution Commemoration Day parade and speech team (Resolution) (1) The Municipal Publicity Department should issue an order to all levels of the Party to fully mobilize and carry out propaganda. (2) District propaganda committee members should convene the propaganda committee members of each district branch to explain the importance of setting out to carry out propaganda in May. (3) District propaganda committee members should assess the performance of each team on the day of departure for propaganda, and those who work hard should be rewarded. (4) If the entire parade and speech team fails to set out for propaganda without a valid reason, the district propaganda committee member should issue a warning; if a team member fails to set out for propaganda without a valid reason, the district branch propaganda committee member should issue a warning. (5) How should party departments at all levels be punished for failing to send representatives to the commemoration ceremonies? (Resolution) Handle in accordance with the Measures for Restricting Party Members from Attending Revolutionary Commemoration Day Gatherings Without a Valid Reason. (6) Many lecture meetings of the district branches in this city have failed to be held as scheduled. How should we try to supervise them? (Resolution) (1) The Municipal Publicity Department should issue an order to all levels of the Party to implement it. (2) Strictly enforce the penalties in the Provisional Regulations for Lecture Meetings. (3) Each district should hold more special lecture meetings. (4) How should a perfect revolutionary drama troupe be organized in this city to facilitate propaganda? (Resolution) Recommend comrades Xu Xingchu, Yang Youwang, and Yang Shaozhi to prepare a plan for discussion at the next meeting. (5) Convene the masses to hold a rally to denounce Yan and Feng for their rebellion. (Resolution) Request the Municipal Publicity Department to review and handle. (6) Each district branch lecture meeting should take the topic of denouncing Yan and Feng as its lecture topic. (Resolution) Request the Municipal Publicity Department to issue an order to all levels of propaganda committee members to implement it conscientiously. (7) Transfer to the Training Department to order all city district branches to use the topic of "Why We Should Denounce the Rebels Yan and Feng" in their discussion meetings. (Resolution) Transfer to the Training Department to order lower-level party departments to hold special discussions on Yan and Feng as quickly as possible. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

The Municipal Public Works Bureau Establishes the Chenjiadu Ferry Office

To regulate water transportation, register, and inspect ships, the Municipal Public Works Bureau has established ferry offices at the Puhui Dongjiadu Wharf and the Xinzhapu Bridge on the Wusong River. However, because the Wusong River is narrow, ships are crowded, and those heading for inspection find it difficult, the bureau decided to establish a ferry office and a boat donation branch at Chenjiadu, where sailboats gather and many ships travel to Chenjiadu and then to Caojiadu and Xiaoshadu without going further. Previously, to facilitate ship merchants, the bureau and the Finance Bureau sent personnel to the area for inspections and to collect donations. However, this was not a long-term solution, so the two bureaus consulted and decided to add a ferry office and a boat donation branch in Chenjiadu, which was approved by the municipal government. The original plan was to build a wooden house and a pier, which is currently being evaluated, but it will take time to complete. To meet current needs, the Finance Bureau has rented a house to establish the boat donation branch, and the Public Works Bureau will use the remaining space to establish the ferry office. It is reported that both will begin operations on May 1st.

A Servant Commits Suicide by Swallowing Opium

Xue Aqi, a 30-year-old native of Nanjing, who worked as a servant, checked into a room at the Xingmao Inn, number 197 Min Ti Ni Yin Road in the French Concession. For unknown reasons, he secretly swallowed raw opium and committed suicide that night. Yesterday morning, the tea server, Tang Changgen, saw that Xue had not yet gotten up, so he went upstairs to call him, but there was no response. He forced the door open and entered the room. Xue had already died on the bed, his body cold. He immediately reported to the police, who sent detectives to investigate the inn. They found traces of raw opium that the deceased had swallowed, and determined that the deceased had committed suicide by taking poison. Since there were no family members, the body was sent to the Tongren Zhuan Yuan Hall for an autopsy. The Criminal Section of the police then reported to Judge Zhu of the French Court, who arrived at the hall at 11:00 AM to confirm that the deceased had indeed committed suicide by taking poison. He ordered photographs to be taken, and Tongren Fuyuan Hall prepared a coffin for burial, awaiting family members to claim the body.

Miscellaneous Opium Cases

French Concession Police Detective Inspector General Shen Defu, Inspectors Chen Sanlin, Detective Lu Jinchen, Mao Jinsheng, Lu Shuixing, etc., discovered that Xu Jinfang's family at 20 Shengping Lane, French Avenue, had privately established an opium den and was secretly selling opium, in violation of the law. They raided the premises the day before yesterday and confiscated 362 pounds of opium, valued at 14,840 yuan, and brought it to the police station. Yesterday, they brought Xu to the French Court for investigation. Xu confessed to privately selling opium. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Xu to a fine of 5,000 yuan, to be confiscated, and the opium was confiscated.

French Concession police detectives discovered that residents Shen Amao and Li Suzhen had privately set up opium dens, providing people with opium lamps for their addiction, in violation of the law and endangering people's lives. They raided their premises the day before yesterday and confiscated lamps and guns, bringing the people to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Court for interrogation and found guilty. The Chinese and Western judges fined both defendants 75 yuan each, to be confiscated as a warning.

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, stating that the Shandong coast, the Yangtze River basin, and the southern coast would be cloudy with fog, or thunderstorms. There was a cyclone around Korea. The winds were gentle and directionless over the Yangtze River basin and the East China Sea. Also, the maximum temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 69.8 degrees, and the minimum was 56.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the maximum was 77.5 degrees, and the minimum was 55.4 degrees.

Death of English Poet Laureate Robert Bridges

Robert Bridges, who was elected Poet Laureate in 1913, died in London on the 21st of this month at the age of eighty-five. He was an eccentric and difficult poet, who earned the honor of being Poet Laureate at the time because of his perseverance, independence, and self-confidence.

He was a doctor in his early years. After leaving Oxford University, he traveled and then went to St. Bartholomew's in London to study medicine and become a military doctor. He also worked as an assistant doctor in a children's hospital and practiced as a doctor. He retired in 1882 and decided to devote himself to literature.

Among the many famous writers in England at the time, Robert Bridges can forever occupy an important position. Although he was a doctor, a skilled doctor who had practiced in hospitals for many years, an inner literary genius had already grown and subdued him. As a result, in 1882 he decided to abandon his medical career and devote himself entirely to literature. When he was appointed Poet Laureate in 1912, he had published very few works, because for many years he had maintained a spirit of perseverance and independence. While others were celebrating and making a big splash, he would silently maintain a period of silence. He had not written a single line of poetry for many years, even though the world was going through an important period, such as the sacrifices made by various countries during the Great War, the commemoration after victory, and the praiseworthy world peace. He ignored all these profound impressions.

At the time, there were many opponents who opposed Bridges' selection as Poet Laureate, saying that such an honor was excessive for him and should be given to Rudyard Kipling, a contemporary English poet, because his talent would never be exhausted at any time. But Bridges remained silent. When he refused to write a poem praising the armistice, he aroused general opposition. He seemed to have his own weapons and was unmoved by those opponents. He said that he was a poet, that poetry was a matter of inspiration, not something to be used as a tool. Let others write what they want to write. As for him, he felt that war was a terrible tragedy and did not arouse the noble emotions that are the foundation of poetry, because it did not inspire him.

His output is small, but the few books of poetry he has are very beautiful, including Eros and Psyche and The Growth of Love. In addition, he has also published two or three memoirs and essays, in which he reveals profound principles of poetry. Recently, he published The Testament of Beauty. (Hui Zi)

The Beauty Testament of Robert Bridges

British Poet Laureate

Poems by Robert Bridges

A long poem written by a Poet Laureate is always noteworthy upon its initial publication, regardless of the opinions of critics or the judgments of posterity. The position of Poet Laureate carries a certain traditional, mythical significance, and the Poet Laureate is considered a representative of the poets of a nation. Although this may not necessarily be the case in reality, especially in modern times, it is a given that a Poet Laureate would not be careless or perfunctory. In ancient times, poets in the king's court were very careful to sing praises, portraying the emperor as the most valiant and virtuous figure in their poems. As for the emperor's character after court, that was not within the poet's jurisdiction and need not be considered. Nowadays, for example in England, although there is still an emperor, that situation is long past. Therefore, there is no need for the Poet Laureate to flatter the emperor. However, nominally, the Poet Laureate is still the emperor's poet. Therefore, the Poet Laureate's poems must still be presented for the emperor's viewing. Because of this relationship, the poet's work must be elegant, honest, pure, and dignified. Therefore, it is natural that the Poet Laureate's poems are known for their beauty rather than ugliness, elegance rather than vulgarity, lofty thoughts, and refined tastes.

The works of British Poet Laureate Robert Bridges are such a thing. His new book, "The Testament of Beauty," is said to be his greatest work and a crown of his own making. This is believable because all of his characteristics are expressed in this work, and expressed to the fullest extent. The elegance of the language, the harmony of the rhythm, the tightness of the structure, and the richness of the style are indeed worthy of praise. However, there is too little emotional content. It is difficult for the reader's emotions to be stirred by it. This work is more like a philosophical treatise or a scripture than a poem. For those who like to cultivate their minds with poetry, this work is very appropriate and valuable. But for those who want to get emotional intoxication from poetry, this work will not be a good fit.

This poem is divided into four books and a prologue. The poem is written in alexandrine (each line has twelve syllables), without rhyme. The whole poem has the refreshing flavor of Milton, but without the dramatic emotion of Milton's epic. The opening seven lines of this poem foreshadow the poem's purpose, which we translate below:

Mankind's "wisdom" is the handmaiden of the divine (gods), and his guesses of the goddess of fate are difficult to predict.

We pass through seas of change, in calm or stormy

Days.

When the ship moves forward, our steadfast will

Shakes like the compass in the compass box.

Our stability is only balance, wisdom lies entirely

In the forceful handling of the invisible.

As for beauty, if people want to obtain the beauty of life, their souls must be infused in God, because God is beauty and love.
